’ рдореИрдирдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢рдЪрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдпрдордкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рджрдордирд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореН ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреЛ рджрд╢ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ рддрддрд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ-’ рдореИрдирдВ рджрдорди рдЖрдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рджреАрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдорд░рдг рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╖рдбреГрдЪрдГ рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ–’ рдореИрдирдордЧреНрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐ рджрд╣реЛ рдорд╛рднрд┐ рд╢реЛрдЪ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреН рдкреВрд╖рд╛ рддреНрд╡реЗрддрд╢реНрдЪреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдпрддреБ рдкреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рем резреж) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рджрд╣реНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░реЗрддрд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╜рдкреНрдпреЗрддрд╛ рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ редред

Jamison Brereton

16 (842)
Agni
Damana Y─Бm─Бyana
24 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 11тАУ14
The focus on the cremation fire in the last part of the preceding hymn (X.15) is enlarged upon here. This fire is seen both as a blessed release of the dead man to the realm of the ancestors and as a menace to the vulnerable dead body. This ambivalence is clearly on display in the first verse, where the fire is begged not to burn up the body, but, on the other hand, to make the dead man тАЬcookedтАЭ and ready to go to the forefathers. The same sentiment is repeated in verse 2, and the journey undertaken. The dead body itself is addressed in verse 3, with its parts consigned to the corresponding cosmic entities. Two more verses to Agni follow (4тАУ5), continuing the themes of verses 1тАУ2. In verses 6тАУ7 the body is addressed again: in verse 6 it is reassured that the physical indignities it has undergone since death will be fixed by the cremation fire and by soma, but in verse 7 it is urged to protect itself against the same fire. The cremation seems to end with verse 8.
With the cremation concluded, the next verses (9тАУ12) treat the inauspicious but powerful cremation fire and the means to render it harmless and to reintegrate it into the generally auspicious sphere of fire. The тАЬflesh-eating fireтАЭ is first explicitly distinguished from тАЬthe otherтАЭ fire, the ritual fire that receives the oblations to the gods, and the flesh-eating fire is assigned the task of taking the sacrifice to the ancestors and bringing them to the sacrifice here. Since this task is parallel to that of the other fire, the godsтАЩ ritual mediator, the negative aspects of the flesh-eating fire can be set aside, and it can be conceptually reconfigured as a positive force, a transformation completed in verse 12.
In the final two verses (13тАУ14) the place where the cremation took place returns to nature, with the fire extinguished and plants growing again. The import of the final apostrophe to a cool and chilly feminine entity is clear, even though the refer ent (a water plant?) is not.

010-019 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton

The next ten hymns (X.10тАУ19) form a Yama cycle, though the subject matter found in the individual hymns is quite various. Yama, the son of Vivasvant, is king of the land of the dead because he was the first mortal to die. Yet he was apparently born immortal (see esp. I.83.5) and chose to become mortal, subject to death, тАЬfor the sake of the gods…and for the sake of offspringтАЭ (X.13.4). The opening hymn in the cycle, the dialogue of Yama and his twin sister Yam─л, on the fraught topic of embarking on incestuous sex in order to produce offspring, addresses YamaтАЩs change of status and his choice, but in a deliberately oblique and misleading fashion, as Yama spurns the sexual advances of his sister, and at the end of their bitter argument there seems little likelihood of children. The last six hymns in this cycle (X.14тАУ19) are collectively known as funeral hymns. The first, X.14, is devoted especially to Yama in his role as king of the realm of the dead, while the others, especially 15тАУ18, concern various aspects of death and the treatment of the deadтАФfor example, the forefathers who preceded us to YamaтАЩs realm in X.15, the cremation fire in X.16, the funeral itself in X.

The intermediate hymns, X.11тАУ13, have less superficially clear connections to the Yama saga, but both X.12 (vss. 6тАУ7) and X.13 (vss. 4тАУ5) make important comments on Yama and on YamaтАЩs choice.

There is also an underlying unifying theme, that of duality and twinned-ness: the absolute disjunction between and the ultimate complementarity and unity of the mortal and the immortal, life and death, men and gods, men and women, heaven and earth, sacred and profane. It is appropriate that the cycle should begin with the dialogue between the primal twins, Yama and Yam─л, whose very names mean тАЬtwinтАЭ and who bridge the gap between mortal and immortal.

English translation:

тАЬAgni, consume him not entirely; afflict him not; scatter not (here and there) his skin nor his body; whenJ─Бtavedas, you have rendered him mature, then send him to the Pitс╣Ыs.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The first six с╣Ыcas are to be recited at (orupon) the death of an initiated person n– d─лkс╣гitamaraс╣Зe; not his skin nor his body: may be an allusion to thespiritual, or suс╣гma ┼Ыar─лra; do not reduce him to ashes, bham─лbh┼лtam m─Б kuru]..

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt burn him through, Agni; donтАЩt scorch him; donтАЩt singe his skin, nor his body.
When you will make him cooked to readiness, J─Бtavedas, then impel him forth to the forefathers.

Griffith

Burn him not up, nor quite consume him, Agni: let not his body or his skin be scattered.
O Jatavedas, when thou hast matured him, then send him on his way unto the Fathers.

Verbrenn ihn nicht, verzehr ihn nicht, o Agni, zersprenge nicht die Haut ihm und die Glieder; Wenn du ihn gar gemacht, o Wesenkenner, dann sollst du ihn zu unsern V├дtern senden.

English translation:

тАЬWhen you have rendered him mature, then give him up, J─Бtavedas, to the Pitс╣Ыs; when he proceedsto that world of spirits, then he becomes subject to the will of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

When he proceeds to that world ofspirits: when he obtains the quickening of life, pr─Бс╣Зa preraс╣Зam, wrought by Agni

Jamison Brereton

When you will have made him cooked to readiness, J─Бtavedas, then deliver him to the forefathers.
When he will embark on the (way) leading to (the other) life, then he will lead at the will of the gods.

Griffith

When thou hast made him ready, Jatavedas, then do thou give him over to the Fathers.
When he attains unto the life that waits him, he shall become the Deities’ controller.

Geldner

Grassmann

Wenn du ihn gar gemacht, o Wesenkenner, dann sollst du ihn den V├дtern ├╝bergeben Wenn er zu jener Geisterwelt gelangt ist, dann soll der G├╢tter Unterthan er werden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the eye repair to the sun; the breath to the wind; go you to the heaven or to the earth, according toyour merit; or go to the waters it it suits you (to be) there, or abide with your members in the plural nts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let your eye go to the sun, your life-breath to the wind. Go to heaven and to earth as is fitting.
Or go to the waters, if it has been fixed for you there. Take your stand in the plants with your limbs.

Griffith

The Sun receive thine eye, the Wind thy spirit; go, as thy merit is, to earth or heaven.
Go, if it be thy lot, unto the waters; go, make thine home in plants with all thy members.

Geldner

In die Sonne soll dein Auge gehen, in den Wind der Lebenshauch, geh in den Himmel und in die Erde nach der Bestimmung! Oder geh ins Wasser, wenn es dir dort beschieden ist; setz dich in den Pflanzen fest mit deinen Gebeinen!

Grassmann

Zur Sonne geh dein Aug’, dein Hauch zum Winde, zur Erd’ und Himmel geh nach deinem Sinne, Geh ins Gew├дsser, wenn’s dir dahin gut d├╝nkt, setz in die Pflanzen dich mit deinen Gliedern.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe unborn portion; burn that, Agni, with your heat; let your flame, your splendour, consume it; withthose glorious members which you have given him, J─Бtavedas, bear him to the world (of the virtuous).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Theunborn portion: ajo bh─Бgaс╕е = the goat is your portion; antarapuruс╣гa, which has no body, no organs of sense;heat, flame and splendour: tapas, ┼Ыocis and arcis: the positive, comparative and superlative radiance of Agni

Jamison Brereton

The goat is your portion. With your heat, heat it up. Let your flame heat it up, let your beam.
The propitious bodies that are yours, o J─Бtavedas, with those convey him to the world of good (ritual) performers.

Griffith

Thy portion is the goat: with heat consume him: let thy fierce flame, thy glowing splendour, burn him
With thine auspicious forms, o Jatavedas, bear this man to the region of the pious.

Geldner

Der Bock ist dein Anteil, den brenne mit deiner Brunst! Den soll deine Glut verbrennen, den deine Flamme! Deine freundlichen Leiber, o Jatavedas, mit denen bef├╢rdere ihn in die Welt der Frommen!

Grassmann

Der Bock geh├╢rt dir, den verbrenn mit Gluten, den m├╢g’ dein Strahl verzehren, den die Flamme; Doch diesen fahr mit deinen Heilsgestalten, o Wesenkenner, hin zum Ort der Frommen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDismiss again to the Pitс╣Ыs, Agni, him who offered on you, comes with the svadh─Бs; putting on(celestial) life, let the remains (of bodily life) depart; let him, J─Бtavedas, be associated with a body.тАЭ

рд╣реЗ рдореГрддрд╢рд░реАрд░ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рдпрджрдЩреНрдЧрдВ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрдГ рд╢рдХреБрдирдГ рдХрд╛рдХрд╛рдЦреНрдпрдГ рдЖрддреБрддреЛрдж рдЖрдЩреАрд╖рджрд░реНрдереЗ рдИрд╖рддреНрддреБрдиреНрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рддрдерд╛ рдкрд┐рдкреАрд▓рдГ рдкрд┐рдкреАрд▓рд┐рдХрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрдкреЛрд╡рд╛ рдЙрддрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдкрд┐рд╡рд╛ рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдкрджрдГ рд╢реНрд╡рд╢реНрд░реГрдЧрд╛рд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдГ рдПрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдордиреНрдпрддрдореЛрдпрджрд┐ рддреБрдиреНрдирд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрддрд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рддрддреНрддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдордЩреНрдЧрдВ рдЕрдЧрджрдВ рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ рджреЛрд╖рд░рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд░реЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕реЛрдорд╢реНрдЪ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд░реВрдкрдГ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рд░реВрдкреЛрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд░реЛрддреБ рдпрдГ рд╕реМрдордГ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдиреН рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЧрд╛рджреАрдиреН рдЖрд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд╛рдиреН рее рем рее рдЕрдиреБрд╕реНрддрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдкрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░реЗрддрд╕реНрдп рдореБрдЦрдордЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрдореЗрддреНрдпрдирдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░реЛрд░реНрдгреБрдпрд╛рддреН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдЮреНрдЪтАФрдЕрдиреБрд╕реНрддрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдкрд╛рдореБ- рддреНрдЦрд┐рджреНрдп рд╢рд┐рд░реЛрдореБрдЦрдВ рдкреНрд░рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдпреЗрджрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрдордкрд░рд┐рдЧреЛрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡реНрдпрдпрд╕реНрд╡реЗрддреАрддрд┐ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShould the black crow, the ant, the snake, the wild beast, harm (a limb) of you, may Agni theall-devourer, and the Soma that has pervaded the br─Бhmaс╣Зas, make it whole.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The wild beast: jackal orhyaena

Jamison Brereton

What of yours the black omen-bird pecked at, or the ant, the serpent, or the dog-footed (beast),
let omnivorous Agni make it free from curse, and Soma, who has
entered the brahmins.

Griffith

What wound soe’er the dark bird hath inflicted, the emmet, or the serpent, or the jackal,
May Agni who devoureth all things heal it and Soma who hath passed into the Brahmans.

Geldner

Was der schwarze Vogel von dir angepickt hat, die Ameise, die Schlange oder ein wildes Tier, das soll der allesfressende Agni heil machen und Soma, der in die Brahmanen eingegangen ist.

Grassmann

Wenn dich gebissen hat der schwarze H├дher, Ameise, Schlange oder auch ein Raubthier, So m├╢ge Agni alles das dir heilen und Soma, der die Priesterschar beseelt hat.

Elizarenkova

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрддреН-рддреЗ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрдГ рд╢рдХреБрдирдГ рдкрд┐рдкреАрд▓рдГ рд╕рд░реНрдкрдГ-рдЙрдд рд╡рд╛ рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдкрджрдГ-рдЖрддреБрддреЛрдж) рд╣реЗ рдЬреАрд╡ ! рдЗрд╕ рд╕рд╛рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд┐рдХ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдпрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛ рдореЗрдВ рдЧреГрдзреНрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрдХреНрд╖реА, рдкрд┐рдкреАрд▓рд┐рдХрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреГрдорд┐, рд╕рд░реНрдкрд╛рджрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдордп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреА рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдШреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХ рдкрд╢реБ рдЬрд┐рд╕-рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧ рдХреЛ рдкреАреЬрд┐рдд рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдХреГрдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рддреН-рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ-рддрддреН-рдЕрдЧрджрдВ рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ рд╕реЛрдордГ-рдЪ рдпрдГ-рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдиреН-рдЖрд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢) рдЙрд╕-рдЙрд╕ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧ рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рднрдХреНрд╖рдХ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╡реЗрддреНрддрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рд╕реЛрдо рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрде рдХрд░ рджреЗрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рееремрее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рд╕реЛрдо рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рднреИрд╖рдЬ рдФрд░ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рднрдпрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдХ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╣реИрдВред рдпрд╣ рдПрдХ рдЖрдпреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд┐рдХ рдФрд░ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХрд╛ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдиреНрдд рд╡рд░реНрдгрд┐рдд рд╣реИред рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп-рдЬреАрд╡рди рдореЗрдВ рднрдпрд╛рдирдХ рдкрдХреНрд╖реА, рдХреГрдорд┐, рд╕рд░реНрдк рдФрд░ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдШреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рднрдп рдФрд░ рдкреАреЬрд╛ рдХрд╛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдг рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ рд╕реЛрдо рд╕реЗ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗред рддрдерд╛ рдЙрдХреНрдд рдЬрдиреНрддреБрдУрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЖрдХреНрд░рдорд┐рдд рдорд░реЗ рд╣реБрдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдХрд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рд╕реЛрдо рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╢рд╡рджрд╣рди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рд░реЛрдЧрд╕рдВрдХреНрд░рд╛рдордХ рдХрд╛рд░рдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдХреНрдпреЛрдВрдХрд┐ рдРрд╕рд╛ рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рдмрд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреА рдЙрдирдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╕рдореНрдкрд░реНрдХ рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдмрдЪ рди рд╕рдХреЗрдВрдЧреЗ рееремрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEnclose the mail of Agni with the (hide of the) cow; cover it with the fat and marrow; then will not(Agni), bold, exulting in his fierce heat, proud, embrace you roundabout to consume you (to ashes).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Make for yourself an enveloping armor against fire with (the flesh of) cows. Cover yourself entirely with grease and fat,
lest the bold one, bristling with his flame, fasten himself around you, intending to utterly burn you up.

Griffith

Shield thee with flesh against the flames of Agni, encompass thee about with fat and marrow,
So will the Bold One, eager to attack thee with fierce glow fail to girdle and consume thee.

Geldner

Mit den Kuhteilen lege dir einen Panzer gegen Agni um, bedecke dich mit Fett und Schmer, auf da├Я dich nicht der dreiste l├╝sterne Agni k├╝hn gemacht, mit seiner Glut umschlinge, um dich zu verbrennen.

Grassmann

Bedecke Agni’s R├╝stung rings mit Butter, umh├╝ll sie ganz mit Fett und Opferschmalze; Nicht soll der kecke, der der Glut sich freuet, dich fest umklammern, um dich zu verbrennen.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЗрдордВ рдЪрдорд╕рдВ рдкреНрд░рдгреАрддрд╛рдкреНрд░рдгрдпрдирдВ рдорд╛рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд░рдГ рдорд╛рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд▓реАрдГ ред рдпрд╢реНрдЪрдорд╕рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛ рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рдЙрддрд╛рдкрд┐рдЪ рд╕реЛрдореНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрд┐рддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ ред рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рдпрдПрд╖рдЪрдорд╕рдГ рджреЗрд╡рдкрд╛рдирдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкрд┐рдмрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рдкрд╛рдирд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпреЛрднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╢реНрдЪрдорд╕реЗ рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдГ рдорд░рдгрд╡рд░реНрдЬрд┐рддрд╛рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкрд┐рддрд░рд╢реНрдЪ рдорд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рд╣рд╡реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд╡реНрдпреИрд╢реНрдЪ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рее рео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, shake not this ladle, for it is dear to the gods and to the (Pitс╣Ыs) who are worthy of the Soma; thiswhich is the drinking ladle of the ogds, in this immortal gods delight.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This beaker here, o AgniтАФdonтАЩt overturn it. It is dear to the gods and to those deserving of soma [=forefathers]тАФ
the beaker that is the drinking vessel of the godsтАФin it the immortal gods find their exhilaration.

Griffith

Forbear, O Agni, to upset this ladle: the Gods and they who merit Soma love it.
This ladle, this which serves the Gods to drink from, in this the Immortal Deities rejoice them.

Geldner

Diesen Becher, o Agni, sollst du nicht umkippen; lieb den G├╢ttern und Somatrinkern ist dieser Becher, aus dem die G├╢tter trinken. Aus diesem zechen die unsterblichen G├╢tter.

Grassmann

Verletze nicht, o Agni, diese Schale, die lieb den G├╢ttern ist und Somapriestern, Dies ist die Schal’, aus der die G├╢tter trinken, aus ihr erlaben sich die ew’gen G├╢tter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI send the flesh-devouring Agni to a distance; let him bearing away sin repair to (the realm of) kingYama; but let this other J─Бtavedas who is known (by all) convey the oblation to the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

King Yama:yamar─Бjyam; this с╣Ыca closes the Pitс╣Ыmeda, or sacrifice to the Pitс╣Ыs

Jamison Brereton

Flesh-eating Agni I send off in the distance. Carrying away defilements, let him go to those who have Yama as king.
Here let only this one, the other J─Бtavedas, carry the oblations to the gods, knowing whatтАЩs ahead.

Griffith

1 send afar flesh eating Agni, bearing off stains may he depart to Yama’s subjects.
But let this other Jatavedas carry oblation to the Gods, for he is skilful.

Geldner

Den fleischfressenden Agni sende ich weit fort; er soll zu den Untertanen K├╢nig Yama┬┤s gehen, das Unreine fortf├╝hrend. Hier soll dieser andere Jatavedas den G├╢ttern das Opfer zuf├╝hren, des Weges kundig!

Grassmann

Den Agni, der das Fleisch verzehrt, entfern’ ich; er geh zum Reich des Jama, Flecken tilgend; Hier aber fahr der andre Wesenkenner den G├╢ttern Opfer zu, die Wege kennend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe flesh-devouring deity Agni, who has entered your dwelling, I turn him out, for the worship of thePitс╣Ыs, upon beholding this other (Agni) J─Бtavedas; let him celebrate the sacrifice (to the Pitс╣Ыs) in the mostexcellent assembly.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The flesh-eating Agni who entered your house, though he saw this one here, the other J─БtavedasтАФ
that god I take for the sacrifice to the forefathers. He will send the
gharma (drink) to the highest seat.

Griffith

I choose as God for Father-worship Agni, flesh-eater, who hath past within your dwelling,
While looking on this other Jatavedas. Let him light flames in the supreme assembly.

Geldner

Der fleischfressende Agni. Der in euer Haus eingedrungen ist, obwohl er diesen anderen Jatavedas sieht, den Gott hole ich weg f├╝r das Manenopfer; er m├╢ge den Gharmatrank an den entferntesten Ort bringen.

Grassmann

Der Fleischverzehrer Agni, der ins Haus drang, erblicke hier den andern Wesenkenner; Zum Ahnenopfer hol’ ich diesen Gott her, er bring’ den heissen Trank zum h├╢chsten Sitze.

тАЬLet Agni the bearer of the Kavya worship the Pitс╣Ыs, who are magnified by truth, let him declare whichare the offerings to the gods, which to the Pitс╣Ыs.тАЭ

The flesh-conveying Agni who will sacrifice to the forefathers, who are strong through truth,
he will proclaim the oblations to the gods and the forefathers.

Griffith

With offerings meet let Agni bring the Fathers who support the Law.
Let him announce oblations paid to Fathers and to Deities.

тАЬLonging we set you down; longing we kindle you; do you longing bring the longing Pitс╣Ыs to eat of the(sacrificial) viands.тАЭ

Eagerly we would install you; eagerly we would kindle you.
Eagerly convey the eager forefathers here, to eat the oblation.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реАрддрд┐рдХреЗ рд╢реАрддрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЗ рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рдордгреНрдбреВрдХреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдордГ-рдЗрдордореН-рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рд╕реБрд╣рд░реНрд╖рдп) рд╣реЗ рд╢реАрддрд░реВрдк рджреВрдм ! рд╣реЗ рд╢реАрддрджреВрдмрдпреБрдХреНрдд рднреВрдореЗ ! рд╣реЗ рдорди рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рд╕реБрдЧрдиреНрдзрд╡рд▓реНрд▓рдХрд┐ ! рд╣реЗ рд╕реБрдЧрдиреНрдзрд╡рд▓реНрд▓рдХрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд рднреВрдореЗ ! рддреВ рдордгреНрдбреВрдХреА рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рднрд▓реА-рднрд╛рдБрддрд┐ рдЗрд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдд рд╣реЛ рдХрд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡ рдХрд╛ рдпрд╣рд╛рдБ рдХреЛрдИ рднреА рдЪрд┐рд╣реНрди рди рд░рд╣реЗ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╢рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН рдЙрд╕ рднреВрдорд┐ рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрдЪрд╛рд░ рдЗрд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реЛрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рд╡рд╣рд╛рдБ рдардгреНрдбреА-рдардгреНрдбреА рджреВрдм рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдЧрдиреНрдзрд▓рддрд╛ рдЙрдЧрдХрд░ рднреВрдорд┐ рд╣рд░реА-рднрд░реА рдФрд░ рдореЗрдгреНрдбрдХрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд▓рдЧреЗ рдПрд╡рдВ рд╢рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡ рдХрд╛ рдХреЛрдИ рднреА рдЪрд┐рд╣реНрди рди рд░рд╣реЗ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реАрддрд┐рдХреЗ рд╢реАрддрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЗ рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рдордгреНрдбреВрдХреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реБ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдордГ-рдЗрдордореН-рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рд╕реБрд╣рд░реНрд╖рдп) рд╣реЗ рд╢реАрддрд┐рдХреЗ рд╢реАрддрд░реВрдкреЗ рджреВрд░реНрд╡реЗ ! тАЬрд╢реАрддрд╛ рджреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдотАЭ [рдзрдиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдирд┐рдШрдгреНрдЯреМ рдкрд░реНрдкрдЯрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд░реНрдЧреЗ рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╡рд╛рдЪрд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпреЗ] тАШрддрддреЛрд╜рдиреБрдХрдореНрдкрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдХрдиреНтАЩред рд╢реАрддрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ ! рд╣реЗ рджреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рднреВрдореЗ ! рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЗ-рдордирдГрдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЗ рд╡рд▓реНрд▓рдХрд┐ ! тАЬрд╡рд▓реНрд▓рдХреАрд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд╛ рд╕реБрд░рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрд╕реНрд░рд╡рд╛ рдЪ рд╕рд╛тАЭ [рдзрдиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдирд┐рдШрдгреНрдЯреМ] рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐-рд╣реЗ рд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рднреВрдореЗ ! рдордгреНрдбреВрдХреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣ рд╕реБ рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдордГ-рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╕реНрд╡ рддрдереЗрдордордЧреНрдирд┐рдордЧреНрдирд┐рдкреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡рдВ рд╕реБрд╣рд░реНрд╖рдп-рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрд▓реАрдХрдВ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реБ, тАЬрд╣реГрд╖реБ-рдЕрд▓реАрдХреЗтАЭ [рднреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдГ] реерезрекрее
